<div id="review_561224587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561224587" />
    <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads"><img alt="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578074503p2/8524618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561224587?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads">Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561224587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5805642774786335446"><a href='http://www.angiesdreamyreads.com/2013/04/blog-tour-twisted-perfection-by-abbi.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review was Posted at Angie's Dreamy Reads</a><br/><br/><i> HUGE giveaway posted right now for an iPad mini and two ebook copies of Twisted Perfection by Abbi Glines. This giveaway is INTERNATIONAL </i><br/><br/><b>4 STARS </b><br/><br/>I was really looking forward to Twisted Perfection by Abbi Glines. I loved Woods in the Too Far Series and was ecstatic that he was getting his own book, giving me the chance to indulge in his story. Let me tell you that Woods is <b>HOT</b>. I was stunned by how dirty and pervy he was. As I started reading one of</span>
  <span id="freeText5805642774786335446" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.angiesdreamyreads.com/2013/04/blog-tour-twisted-perfection-by-abbi.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review was Posted at Angie's Dreamy Reads</a><br><br><i> HUGE giveaway posted right now for an iPad mini and two ebook copies of Twisted Perfection by Abbi Glines. This giveaway is INTERNATIONAL </i><br><br><b>4 STARS </b><br><br>I was really looking forward to Twisted Perfection by Abbi Glines. I loved Woods in the Too Far Series and was ecstatic that he was getting his own book, giving me the chance to indulge in his story. Let me tell you that Woods is <b>HOT</b>. I was stunned by how dirty and pervy he was. As I started reading one of my first thoughts was <br><br><b>“HOLY CRAP!! Is this an Abbi Glines book?”!!</b> <br><br>It’s sizzling and steamy right from the start and really doesn't slow down much. Woods is possessive and extremely alpha. He has a dirty mouth that made me at times blush. I’m not sure what I was expecting going in but I was definitely surprised by the sexual explosiveness and intensity it had. <br><br>Abbi writes books that are absolutely addicting. Once you’ve read an Abbi Glines book you’ll be hooked for life. There’s absolutely no turning back. Her books are like crack and her characters always hit very close to home. They’re always relatable and lovable. She has a knack with pulling the readers in and in Twisted Perfection it was no different. You can expect a quick read with hot, intense and swoony characters. <br><br>Della is so broken. She’s a shattered girl trying to find herself in a world she has no idea how to live in. After a torturous childhood Della is given the opportunity by her best friend to go out into the world and “find herself.” She needs to learn to be independent and to find some sort of freedom from a childhood that haunts her every moment. Della just wants to have fun and experience all the ups and downs that go with a normal life. She wants to learn how to <b>LIVE!</b><br><br>Woods is working hard to take over the family business. He want the top job and feels he’s owed it. In order to get where he wants to go he has to make sacrifices. His father has a plan and Woods has to stick with it in order to get what he wants. Woods is tired of someone always controlling his life but being successful is the most important thing to him until he meets Della.<br><br>When Della and Woods lay eyes on each other it’s <b>LUST</b> at first sight. Della is passing through town and needs to stop and get gas. She meets Woods and a scorching one night stand happens that leaves a long lasting impression on them both. A couple month’s later when Della has to return to town after an unfortunate situation occurred she meets Woods again and sparks fly. The attraction is <b>UNDENIABLE</b> and the chemistry is <b>ADDICTIVE</b>. They can’t stay or keep their hands off each other. But Della has a mountain of issues and Woods has some problems of his own. These two have a lot to work through before anything long lasting could ever truly happen. It’s an angsty hot mess but one that works brilliantly.<br><br>Overall I really liked the book. The only thing I wished was that the pacing was slowed down a tad and that the characters were a little more developed. Other than that I still felt that Abbi kept us on the edge of our seats waiting to find out what Woods was going to do and what Della’s secrets were. The ending is......well another cliffhanger but in my honest opinion it’s <b>NOTHING</b> that should hold you back from reading the book. I can’t wait to see what happens in the next book Simple Perfection. Woods and Della are amazing together.<br><br><b>
  <u>MY WOODS</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380311465i/688460._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>

<span id="freeTextContainer3592704552609490401">I'm not sure about Twisted but Woods sure was <b>Perfection</b>....<i>on a stick</i>!   <span id="freeText3592704552609490401" style="display:none">I'm not sure about Twisted but Woods sure was <b>Perfection</b>....<i>on a stick</i>! I was looking forward to Woods' story because you just knew it would be good especially with the way Woods takes care of people and he's just so intense! AG did not disappoint. <br><br>Della was innocent and sweet...I even wanted to help her. It really was quite hard to hear everything that she went through and is still working out.               <span id="reviewTextContainer536709991" class="readable"

When I first met you in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16070903.Fallen_Too_Far__Too_Far___1_" title="Fallen Too Far (Too Far, #1) by Abbi Glines" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen Too Far</a> I just knew I was going to love you. Boy did you surpass my wildest hopes with your possesive, sexy, and dirty-talkin ways.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408307ra/798685.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story starts off with a bang...and I do mean a bang<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408307ra/798686.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It starts hot and doesn't let off until the very end. Abbi Glines is seriously the queen of writing one hell of a steamy love scene. Seriously Ms. Glines<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408307ra/798687.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But I digress<br><br>Della sets off on a road trip to see the world, while trying to heal and learn to live with the wounds of a dark and troubling childhood. When she stops at a gas station to fill up her car and meets Woods.<br><br>Woods you truly had me at <blockquote>
  <i>"You're gonna have to let me get around you, sweetheart."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Woods is trying to escape his own demons, and meeting Della offers him a necessary distraction.<br><br>I don't want to reveal too much of what happens next, since it will take away from the story, but it kept me up reading all night.<br><br>Certain events take place and Della finds herself meeting Woods again. Only this time, Woods isn't letting her go.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You are mine. Do you hear me? You are mine, Della Sloane. I will take care of you. Nothing is taking you away from me. Nothing."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I loved the way that Woods and Della's relationship develops. Yes there is some angst, and there were some times that I wanted to smack Woods. Thankfully, it didn't take him long for him to get his act together.<br><br>I will say that this book had some of the steamiest scenes I've read in a book by Abbi Glines. I loved Rush, and I adored Preston from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15778138.Just_for_Now__Sea_Breeze___4_" title="Just for Now (Sea Breeze, #4) by Abbi Glines" rel="nofollow noopener">Just for Now</a>, but 20% in, I was saying "Preston and Rush, who?"<br><br>Not a spoiler, but some dirty talkin' lovin'*<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <blockquote>
    <i> "Are you gonna come in my mouth?" he asked sticking out his tongue and running it from my opening to my swollen clit.<br>"I need to." I panted.<br>"This pretty little pussy needs to come?" he asked, taking another long leisurely lap with his tongue.</i>
  </blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>When I first read a blurb about Della, I was concerned that she would grate on me. I was afraid that it would be the case of a broken, needy, and whiny heroine. She was certainly not that. She has her demons, but she's no pushover and I really enjoyed her character.<br><br>I thought that this book would be a stand alone, so I got to admit that the ending left me feeling a little...well...let's go with confused?<br><br>It did leave off on a bit of a cliffhanger, but it is not one I can't live with since the main relationship between the hero and heroine WAS resolved.<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText8314735046801403238" style="display:none">It has been a while since I read Rosemary Beach series. I remember the first 2 series, I have fond memories about it. The twist and turn and the soap opera drama reminds me of that Beverly Hills premium soap opera back when I was teeneager. <br /><br />Then I guess ny taste in romance is also revolving. When I picked up Twisted Perfection, I cringed. Characters are bad. Immature, stupid and just dumb. The plot is even ridiculous. Only the steamy smut is still tolerable. And even with that, there are not much of smut scenes in this book. <br /><br />There is no real/ vulnerable attraction between Wood and Della. I can not stand Della. She wants to be free and by doing sex with random strangers. When she found out those strangers actually have commitment with others woman, she freaks out. Good God! <br /><br />Well for what is worth, I picked up this book because it is Rosemary Beach after all. <br /><br />2 stars</span>

        <a title="Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~" href="/user/show/3758447-vikki-squee-lite">Vikki ~ *squee* lite ~</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17326749987136994300">I enjoyed this a whole bunch more then the Rush/Blaire saga, in a large part because Woods consistently put Delilah first. For all his talk, I didn't feel the same about Rush. <br/><br/>There is nothing I would change about Woods - he was hot, sweet, understanding and all around amazing. He was exactly what Delilah needed. We once again have the case of insta-lust which quickly leads to almost-but-not-quite insta love. I'm choosing to ignore that you probably shouldn't be ready to uproot your entire life </span>
  <span id="freeText17326749987136994300" style="display:none">I enjoyed this a whole bunch more then the Rush/Blaire saga, in a large part because Woods consistently put Delilah first. For all his talk, I didn't feel the same about Rush. <br /><br />There is nothing I would change about Woods - he was hot, sweet, understanding and all around amazing. He was exactly what Delilah needed. We once again have the case of insta-lust which quickly leads to almost-but-not-quite insta love. I'm choosing to ignore that you probably shouldn't be ready to uproot your entire life for someone after a couple of weeks, but maybe I'm just being cynical. <br /><br />It felt like Abbi Glines actually upped the steam factor again with this one. I gotta admit, it got an eyebrow raise or two out of me. I'm not complaining at all - but I'm curious how much farther she is going to push it. <br /><br />The ending was the kind of cliffhanger I like. It made me curious about what is in store next for Delilah and woods, but didn't make me want to cry/throw things. Looking forward to the rest of their story.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the whole confirmation of the Grant/Nan pairing had me vomiting a little in my mouth. I am so not looking forward to that book  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>

<div id="review_526749321" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526749321" />
    <a title="*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time"><img alt="*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460037460p2/9072385.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/526749321?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time" class="user" itemprop="url" name="*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time" href="/user/show/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time">*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526749321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer495073372973964281">First and foremost, as previosuly mentioned.....<br/><br/>Woods<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/429028.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Woods really won me over in Never Too Far but if I am being completely honest I was a little disppointed with Twisted Perfection. I found it to be too much like the Fallen series...<br/><br/>Broken girl who doesn't think she's good enough for the guy + hot rich guy that shouldn't be with the girl but can't stay away from her. Problems arise and the girl ends up back where she came from. With that being said, I do think I liked Della's character a bit be</span>
  <span id="freeText495073372973964281" style="display:none">First and foremost, as previosuly mentioned.....<br><br>Woods<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/429028.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Woods really won me over in Never Too Far but if I am being completely honest I was a little disppointed with Twisted Perfection. I found it to be too much like the Fallen series...<br><br>Broken girl who doesn't think she's good enough for the guy + hot rich guy that shouldn't be with the girl but can't stay away from her. Problems arise and the girl ends up back where she came from. With that being said, I do think I liked Della's character a bit better than Blaire's. <br><br>Della's past was brutal. Forced to live in seclusion by her crazy mom, Della finds herself on the road to self-discovery. Along the way, she meets Woods....at a gas station, where she has no clue how to pump gas (I haven't really decided how believable this is). <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398981ra/771570.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They experience an explosive night together and then go their separate ways. 4 months later Della finds herself back in Rosemary working at the club for Woods....I mean what are the odds really?!?! But guess what...Woods is engaged to marry another woman!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408189ra/798376.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Luckily he realizes the error of his ways rather quickly and breaks things off....afterall the engagement was what daddy Kerrington wanted not Woods. I liked Woods and Della together....Della lives in constant fear of turning in to her mother. She has nightmares and anxiety attacks...and Woods was so good and patient with her. <br><br>The ending....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/474073.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was a little predictable I think....I pretty much saw that coming and once again it was eerily similar to the Fallen series <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ with Blaire fleeing back to her hometown...the only difference being that she ends up with Woods at the end where Blaire turned Rush away.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>Unfortunately, this is going to once again be a two book series. I had to dock some stars for this....I wanted it to be a stand-alone. It could have been a stand-alone. The ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with the dad having a heart-attack just as soon as Woods tells him to f*ck off. Really?!?! Why?!?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>...ugh! Just give me a nice little epilogue or something. <br><br>Bottomline, I did enjoy the book and read it in a matter of hours (it was pretty short) and if you liked the Fallen series then you will like the Perfection series as well. It was also nice to see some of the supporting characters from the Fallen series return in this book. <br><br>I will leave everyone with one last thought....I imagine this was Woods as a baby! :)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380408189i/798377.jpg" width="250" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="495073372973964281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_548160632" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548160632" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548160632?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548160632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12669148285596906228"><i>
  <b>They say a picture is worth a thousand words….<br/> so what’s this .gif worth?</b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411463ra/808239.gif' alt=' photo headdesk1_zpsf26a1d0a.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>Having read almost all of GLINES’ contemporary stuff, I knew what was in store for in picking this: sad girl, rich boy. No, let’s be specific here: There’s a girl of the sad and scarred variety lacking experience because of said sad/scarred life. There’s also a rich boy /man prone to being the alpha complete with ‘He roared this then he growled that.’ (I’m serious here, folks.) <br/><br/>There’s also the multiple layers of dr</span>
  <span id="freeText12669148285596906228" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>They say a picture is worth a thousand words….<br> so what’s this .gif worth?</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411463ra/808239.gif" alt=" photo headdesk1_zpsf26a1d0a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><br>Having read almost all of GLINES’ contemporary stuff, I knew what was in store for in picking this: sad girl, rich boy. No, let’s be specific here: There’s a girl of the sad and scarred variety lacking experience because of said sad/scarred life. There’s also a rich boy /man prone to being the alpha complete with ‘He roared this then he growled that.’ (I’m serious here, folks.) <br><br>There’s also the multiple layers of drama that I just could not buy. For one, she’s running away from her past to “discover” herself (it’s something I could have liked too, but need she have ended up in someone’s bed time and again?) For him, it’s a father who’s overbearing and bent on him following a certain path… I didn’t get this because for such a tough guy you’d think he think he is… well, he just wasn’t. (Tough, I mean… or smart, for that matter.) Then finally for them, it’s that pull that they can’t help (again)… how she’s made for him and he for her, but there are things in the way and blablabla, like how she’s a past she’s yet to reveal, and how he has a certain future to get to, then how he thinks she’s a certain way and she thinks he’s a certain way…. only for both of them to find that they’re way off base. <br><br>Plus there’s the whole thing on a girl with little experience managing to rock his world on every single encounter (and him for her too!) I mean, really now.. . shouldn’t it suffice that’s she’s pretty and he’s hot? Must they be gods and goddesses between the sheets, too? Apparently so… this is about the only aspect I bought. If titillation was the goal, then the same has been met. It’s on this note that Glines has upped the ante... in much more steamy detail. Unfortunately, it was the type of detail that wasn’t working for me. Because without fail, each sad moment here is concluded with them bumping uglies and me hot/bothered (what? I’m being honest here!) but still wondering what the hell they saw in each other to begin with. She’s a mess and he’s a douche; she wants what’s best for him and he wants to fix her... there’s a moment here when he declares with a passion to find a cure for her that had me rolling my eyes and getting a head ache in exchange. <br><br>So sad girl, rich boy with the either one or the other saving the other from themselves or each other.. who knows? More on him either growling/declaring/roaring that she’s mine mine mine and then them managing to get each other off multiple times in a single occasion. So take all that together, well… this wasn’t <s>bad… </s> Oh! who am I kidding? <b>I hated this.</b><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12669148285596906228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NJp/t1rk2K4xFRxM5oDE2akAzk5L9gD91kRHnTVjD/nMbOOKK2HdyACqsVaTEb3aw4x+9w/XHPOTBI/EsD8+Hg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PbFcIaWGcQ2MFCccYN16GELumzfgbZmd8evvwIxPJpbFR8Ac1AN0a72rigYVTAMbKGIrjqRMhZO0qyeZCRMXcQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer6506002195540023483">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be Britis</span>
  <span id="freeText6506002195540023483" style="display:none">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be British but alas she was born in Alabama. When asked how many books she has written she has to stop and count on her fingers. When she’s not locked away writing, she is reading, shopping (major shoe and purse addiction), sneaking off to the movies alone, and listening to the drama in her teenagers lives while making mental notes on the good stuff to use later. Don’t judge.<br /><br />You can connect with Abbi online in several different ways. She uses social media to procrastinate.<br /></span>
